<span id="freeTextContainer6695508396287566101">Nore Roberts didn't ask for a new life, but now that her mom is gone and her dad is newly married, she has to settle in at Shadow Grove, the old Civil War mansion her stepfamily calls home. When she meets her stepmother, Lisette, Nore is shocked by her youth and beauty that gives her chills- and a hint of something sinister. There's hope of becoming friends with her stepbr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6695508396287566101">Nore Roberts didn't ask for a new life, but now that her mom is gone and her dad is newly married, she has to settle in at Shadow Grove, the old Civil War mansion her stepfamily calls home. When she meets her stepmother, Lisette, Nore is shocked by her youth and beauty that gives her chills- and a hint of something sinister. There's hope of becoming friends with her stepbrother and sister, until Nore realizes they're hiding something. When she begins to feel like the target of a deadly plan, Nore starts digging into her stepfamily's past. The skeletons in their closet are more real than she ever imagined. Can Nore expose her stepmother's dark secret before an old and evil magic swallows her up?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6695508396287566101">...more</a>

<h3 class="communityQuestionSubTitle">

<div class="communityQuestion">
<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/431805-the-blurb-sounds-very-cryptic-but-is-this">The blurb sounds very cryptic, but is this actual fantasy or paranormal?
If it is, is this book very paranormal or just has paranormal elements?</a>
</div>
<div class="communityQAFooter questionFooter">
<ul class="questionFooterActions">
<li class="footerItem like">
<span id="like_container_community_question_431805" class="likeItContainer"><a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F47751.Locked_in_Time" class="jsLike like_it" rel="nofollow">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp">

</li>

<div class="allCommunityAnswers">
<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/36496531-suzana-thompson" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/36496531-suzana-thompson">Suzana Thompson</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is paranormal. I'm not sure what you mean by very paranormal, but it's about a girl discovering paranormal secrets about her new stepmother and<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is paranormal. I'm not sure what you mean by very paranormal, but it's about a girl discovering paranormal secrets about her new stepmother and her children. I don't want to give anything away, but it's not about vampires or werewolves or anything that is so prevalent in supernatural stories today.<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('_tip_292').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

  <a href="/user/show/4872818-misty-ronchietto" class="left imgcol" title="Misty Ronchietto"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Misty Ronchietto" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/395375563?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 19, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4872818-misty-ronchietto" class="user" title="Misty Ronchietto">Misty Ronchietto</a>

          added it




        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4872818-misty-ronchietto?shelf=ty-s-ar-books" class="actionLinkLite">ty-s-ar-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer395375563">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6204614574978789436">I'm reading all of my son's AR (for school) books with him so we can discuss and I can make sure he is actually reading rather than just flipping pages. Haha. He hasn't finished yet so it will be interesting to get his perspective. <br /><br />The book was interesting and fast paced enough to keep one reading but I had a few major issues with it. <br /><br />First, the entire book is premised on the idea that the only thing of concern for the female characters is maintaining or achieving physical beauty for the purpose</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6204614574978789436">I'm reading all of my son's AR (for school) books with him so we can discuss and I can make sure he is actually reading rather than just flipping pages. Haha. He hasn't finished yet so it will be interesting to get his perspective. <br /><br />The book was interesting and fast paced enough to keep one reading but I had a few major issues with it. <br /><br />First, the entire book is premised on the idea that the only thing of concern for the female characters is maintaining or achieving physical beauty for the purpose of keeping or attracting men. As a parent, I think this is a dangerous message for our sons and daughters. My poor son will be getting an earful of redirection once he's done with the book. <br /><br />Second, Nore, Is a completely one dimensional character. We know almost nothing about her other than the fact that her mom died and she got shipped off to boarding school by her absentee father. She also manages to, inexplicably, maintain respect for a father who has very little regard for her physical and emotional well being. <br /><br />Third, Nore's dad is an immature, selfish bastard and terrible father whose inexcusable neglect of his daughter is entirely ignored throughout the book. The fact that Nore never called him on it frustrated me to no end. <br /><br />Amusing enough as a high concept read for preteens. However, portrayal of gender roles in this book seems to be locked in time well before women had any self respect apparently. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6204614574978789436">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3485387721562800117">This is my least-favorite of Lois Duncan's books. It's also the only one I DIDN'T read as a teen since it was published after I had graduated from the YA section (and yes, there was a YA section at my library back in those olden days. YA DID exist pre-Twilight, you know). I don't know if this one packs less of a punch than her earlier works because it was written later in her career, or if Lois Duncan is best read when one is young and just discovering supernatural suspense fiction.<br /><br />I still LOVE</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3485387721562800117">This is my least-favorite of Lois Duncan's books. It's also the only one I DIDN'T read as a teen since it was published after I had graduated from the YA section (and yes, there was a YA section at my library back in those olden days. YA DID exist pre-Twilight, you know). I don't know if this one packs less of a punch than her earlier works because it was written later in her career, or if Lois Duncan is best read when one is young and just discovering supernatural suspense fiction.<br /><br />I still LOVE <a title="Summer of Fear by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/477990.Summer_of_Fear">Summer of Fear</a> and <a title="Stranger with My Face by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/838768.Stranger_with_My_Face">Stranger with My Face</a> and <a title="Down a Dark Hall by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/538757.Down_a_Dark_Hall">Down a Dark Hall</a> but when I reread them now I am transported back to when I read them as a kid, and can remember and revisit the thrills and chills and fascination I felt then. This one? Eh, it was OK.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_87303613">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/87303613" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/50378-angie" class="left imgcol" title="Angie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1260221213p2/50378.jpg" alt="Angie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/87303613?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/50378-angie" class="user" title="Angie">Angie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=good-uns" class="actionLinkLite">good-uns</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=nostalgireads" class="actionLinkLite">nostalgireads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya" class="actionLinkLite">ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer87303613">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11729905668904831906">So I've talked about my <a title="Joan Lowery Nixon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/129033.Joan_Lowery_Nixon">Joan Lowery Nixon</a> phase before. I actually think I discovered <a title="Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">Lois Duncan</a> right before Nixon, but the two will always go hand and hand in my mind. Together they perfectly satisfied my twelve-year-old thirst for a light blending of suspense and the macabre. And no Duncan book did that better than the deliciously creepy LOCKED IN TIME. I enjoyed all of her books and they all succeeded in giving me the chills at one point or another. My old copy of <a title="I Know What You Did Last Summer by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47763.I_Know_What_You_Did_Last_Summer">I Know What You Did Last S</a></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11729905668904831906">So I've talked about my <a title="Joan Lowery Nixon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/129033.Joan_Lowery_Nixon">Joan Lowery Nixon</a> phase before. I actually think I discovered <a title="Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">Lois Duncan</a> right before Nixon, but the two will always go hand and hand in my mind. Together they perfectly satisfied my twelve-year-old thirst for a light blending of suspense and the macabre. And no Duncan book did that better than the deliciously creepy LOCKED IN TIME. I enjoyed all of her books and they all succeeded in giving me the chills at one point or another. My old copy of <a title="I Know What You Did Last Summer by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47763.I_Know_What_You_Did_Last_Summer">I Know What You Did Last Summer</a> is definitely showing its age and my love, as I loved revisiting those characters the most. But LOCKED IN TIME is the one that truly scared me. Not just chills, not just anxious anticipation, but the real deal, had me setting the book down long enough to calm my racing heart kind of scared. <br /><br />Seventeen-year-old Nore has been away at boarding school since her mother died a year ago. Now she's on her way to Louisiana to visit her father and his new wife and her two children. When she arrives at Shadow Grove, several things are clear. Her father is happy with his new life. Her stepmother Lisette, stepbrother Gabe, and stepsister Josie are perfectly well-mannered and perfectly beautiful. And something is very, very wrong with them. Through conversations she has with elderly neighbors and residents of the town, Nore's seemingly crazy suspicions about Lisette, Gabe, and the entire Berge family start to grow. These vaguely horrific suspicions grow stronger as she overhears them discuss events from decades ago as though they were there when they happened. Nore finds herself torn between her distrust of Lisette and her growing friendship with Gabe. Determined to make her father come to his senses and see the truth, Nore rushes to solve the mystery of her new family before her time at Shadow Grove runs out.<br /><br />When I think about this story now, years since I last re-read it, I am still instantly filled with the same overwhelming emotions--an appreciation for the heady beauties of the Deep South mixed with a sense of impending doom. Ms. Duncan struck the perfect chord with the impossibly lovely Berges and the simultaneous fear and longing Nore feels when in the presence of a "real" family again. The truth to the mystery unfolds smoothly and slowly, like warm molasses, creeping up behind you to tap you on the shoulder. In some ways it reminded me of a younger, simpler <a title="Mary Stewart" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart">Mary Stewart</a> novel, with its lovely heroine and its beautiful atmosphere. I remember thinking Nore was brave and being desperate for someone to believe her, for Gabe not to really be trying to kill her, for her father, in his grief, not to have ruined them both so thoroughly. It's the same emotional connection I seek out today when I'm in the mood for something slightly dangerous, slightly haunting, slightly bittersweet. It was these early young adult mysteries that led me to the <a title="Mary Stewart" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15590.Mary_Stewart">Mary Stewart</a>s, the <a title="Laurie R. King" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6760.Laurie_R__King">Laurie King</a>s, the <a title="Deanna Raybourn" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/156327.Deanna_Raybourn">Deanna Raybourn</a>s I discovered later on. I will always love them for being the beginning. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11729905668904831906">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer16008642646541866053">Fun fact: this is easily my favorite Lois Duncan book and it was the first one I read.<br /><br />It's just as suspenseful as her others, but it also is a little more Gothic. There's a big question (at least as I read it) about how much is real and how much is in Nore's imagination. (I love stories like that, where you're not entirely sure what the true story is.)<br /><br />And when I re-read it for this feature, it was so much scarier than I remembered it being. I feel like one of the creepiest things is the fact tha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16008642646541866053">Fun fact: this is easily my favorite Lois Duncan book and it was the first one I read.<br /><br />It's just as suspenseful as her others, but it also is a little more Gothic. There's a big question (at least as I read it) about how much is real and how much is in Nore's imagination. (I love stories like that, where you're not entirely sure what the true story is.)<br /><br />And when I re-read it for this feature, it was so much scarier than I remembered it being. I feel like one of the creepiest things is the fact that you can know something WRONG is happening but no one will believe you. *shiver*<br /><br />It's also interesting to see just how quickly things can go from normal and happy to batshit insane and scary.<br /><br />Highly recommended.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9023068360142561725">Lois Duncan is good with building atmosphere, both environmental and emotional. The story was set in Louisiana and the descriptions of the surroundings and even the weather were very well done. Duncan also created a very creepy feeling from the very beginning, but I found the foreshadowing to be a bit heavy-handed.<br /><br />I might have really liked this book had I read it when I was in middle school. It doesn't seem childish or anything, but maybe shallow is how I would describe it. There's not much dept</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9023068360142561725">Lois Duncan is good with building atmosphere, both environmental and emotional. The story was set in Louisiana and the descriptions of the surroundings and even the weather were very well done. Duncan also created a very creepy feeling from the very beginning, but I found the foreshadowing to be a bit heavy-handed.<br /><br />I might have really liked this book had I read it when I was in middle school. It doesn't seem childish or anything, but maybe shallow is how I would describe it. There's not much depth to any of the characters and no real exploration of the implications of the strange secret the Berge' family hides.<br /><br />In all, it wasn't a bad read, but I feel like it could have been more than it was. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer6965276712594924158">Nore's mom died and she's shocked to discover that her father has suddenly remarried a new woman while she's been away. Furthermore, Lisette is a bit too perfect, as are her teenage kids. Nore's mother comes to her in dreams trying to urge her and her father to escape the stepfamily, but she has no power, and everyone is bamboozled by these creepy strangers. Furthermore, they keep making comments that either make it clear they're hiding something or imply they have been alive for more than 100 y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6965276712594924158">Nore's mom died and she's shocked to discover that her father has suddenly remarried a new woman while she's been away. Furthermore, Lisette is a bit too perfect, as are her teenage kids. Nore's mother comes to her in dreams trying to urge her and her father to escape the stepfamily, but she has no power, and everyone is bamboozled by these creepy strangers. Furthermore, they keep making comments that either make it clear they're hiding something or imply they have been alive for more than 100 years. What do they want with her dad and what is going to happen to her when she finds out their secrets?<br /><br />There are a couple clichés in this book--the random premonition gets ignored and turns out to be true, of course, and the creepy step-family has a terrible secret--and there wasn't a whole lot that was new brought to the table when the idea of living beyond a normal human lifespan is tackled in this book. But Lois Duncan is good at making reactions visceral and making you care about people even if they're in predictable situations. It's a little murky on the details sometimes, for a mystery, but some readers will still get invested no problem.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6965276712594924158">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_858160780">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858160780" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5783023-halcyon-daze" class="left imgcol" title="Halcyon Daze"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1386238990p2/5783023.jpg" alt="Halcyon Daze" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/858160780?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5783023-halcyon-daze" class="user" title="Halcyon Daze">Halcyon Daze</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=three-star" class="actionLinkLite">three-star</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=gothic" class="actionLinkLite">gothic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=lois-duncan" class="actionLinkLite">lois-duncan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer858160780">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15609990314332881335"><strong>Plot:</strong><br /><br />Nore Robbins spends the summer in down south Louisiana in order to get acquainted with her new step-family. She's a bit bitter that her father decided to remarry so soon after her mother's death, but tries to approach her step-mom and step-siblings with an open mind. Step-mom is a beautiful woman named Lisette Berge who has a teenage son named Gabe who clearly has the hots for his new stepsister and a young daughter named Josie, who's a sullen thirteen-year-old prone to throwing tantrums. T</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15609990314332881335"><strong>Plot:</strong><br /><br />Nore Robbins spends the summer in down south Louisiana in order to get acquainted with her new step-family. She's a bit bitter that her father decided to remarry so soon after her mother's death, but tries to approach her step-mom and step-siblings with an open mind. Step-mom is a beautiful woman named Lisette Berge who has a teenage son named Gabe who clearly has the hots for his new stepsister and a young daughter named Josie, who's a sullen thirteen-year-old prone to throwing tantrums. They live in Shadow Grove, an old plantation home with a lot history.<br /><br />Nore quickly realizes that there's something off about her step-family. For example, they claim to be at events that they couldn't possibly have attended and purposefully isolate themselves from the rest of society and have a strange aversion to technology. Then events take a drastic turn when they try to kill her.<br /><br /><strong>Review:</strong><br /><br />This is another one of Lois Duncan's teen Gothic books, and it's pretty good in that regard. We have all the right elements - beautiful, mysterious house in the middle of nowhere, beautiful heroine trying to flee from danger, a family hiding a dark secret. The setting is very atmospheric and heavy, going for the genteel South vibe. I loved the descriptions, from the food to Shadow Grove to basically everything. So in that aspect, it's well done.<br /><br />The mystery is pretty easy to solve, right in your face, and it can be frustrating when the book drags it on when it's so OBVIOUS to you as the reader. Otherwise, the pacing is good and it's a light, easy read.<br /><br />But the most frustrating thing would have to be Chuck Robbins, our heroine's father. Chuck is pretty smitten with his new wife and basically stands up for her and his new step-children every time they get into a confrontation/fight with Nore. I don't know about you guys, but I like to believe that if my otherwise pleasant, well-adjusted daughter started bringing up valid points about how overall weird my new spouse was, I wouldn't snap back at her and accuse her of lying or imagining things. Chuck remarries mere months after Nore's mother's death, and while I personally don't see anything wrong with that, I completely understand Nore's apprehension, particularly since Chuck just married out of the blue and sent his daughter (who he shipped off to boarding school, by the way) a letter saying, "By the way, I got married! Sorry I didn't tell you sooner!" And then basically guilt trips Nore into accepting his marriage in the beginning of the book. Classy move there, Chuck. He also says he wants to reconnect with Nore after the whole tragedy with her mother's death, but throughout the book he's way too wrapped up in his work or his new wife to actually sit down and have a proper conversation with his daughter.<br /><br />I didn't like Chuck, if you can tell.<br /><br />Now, on to more serious issues. Re-reading as someone older and wiser, I found certain problems with it that I hadn't noticed as a young teen. (Slight spoilers to follow.)<br /><br />There's a portrayal of voodooism in the book that's really vilified and stereotypical as the strange, barbaric religion practiced by those (probably black, Native, or mixed) Cajuns. Also, in the backstory, there's an affair between a white slaveowner and a Cajun woman, and it's portrayed as that evil, seducing, voodoo-practicing Cajun woman's fault. This is so terrible on so many levels. In real life, it was these white men taking advantage of these poor women, not this drivel.<br /><br />Also, just as a warning, the character of Lisette Berge is racist. She talks flippantly about how cheap slave labor was back in the day and once bitterly accuses a Cajun girl of being promiscuous simply because she's Cajun.<br /><br />And for this reason, this is a three star book instead of four stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15609990314332881335">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_124868337">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124868337" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/563372-susan" class="left imgcol" title="Susan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1251322041p2/563372.jpg" alt="Susan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/124868337?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 07, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/563372-susan" class="user" title="Susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3605639-locked-in-time" title="Hardcover 9780316195553" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/563372-susan?shelf=home" class="actionLinkLite">home</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer124868337">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5083636657782116816">I would have starred this higher if I was teenager reading it as I think I would have enjoyed it much more at about twelve. Duncan is a good writer and I plan to read more of her mysteries, but this was a just a bit too predictable. I don't think it was supposed to be a huge surprise but I figured out the mystery almost immediately, taking away some of the punch later on. However, she build tension slowly, the characters are relatively interesting and creepy, and I loved the setting (south Louis</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5083636657782116816">I would have starred this higher if I was teenager reading it as I think I would have enjoyed it much more at about twelve. Duncan is a good writer and I plan to read more of her mysteries, but this was a just a bit too predictable. I don't think it was supposed to be a huge surprise but I figured out the mystery almost immediately, taking away some of the punch later on. However, she build tension slowly, the characters are relatively interesting and creepy, and I loved the setting (south Louisiana). It was the perfect lush, historical, eerie locale for a mystery.<br /><br />Course evaluation: Duncan skillfully presents an intriguing mystery with supernatural undercurrents. Though some of the dialogue and references are dated (such as the opening of a new disco in town), readers will still be able to enjoy the suspense and building tension of the plot. The south Louisiana locale is the perfect setting for the sinister story; voodoo plays a large part in the family’s secret, Nore feels out of place in Creole culture, and the environment (shady trees, strange flowers, foreboding river) itself add to the air of mystery in the story. Duncan leaves the ending slightly open for the reader to guess how Josie and Nore’s futures will pan out but does give the reader some closure on the climactic events of the plot.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5083636657782116816">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1381360974">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8557161482196380224">If I had to choose a favourite book, from my mid to late teens, this one would be a very serious contender. I recall picking this up, at the local library, imagining it to be some kind of history book from the title. It looked intriguing enough to take home and read so I did. I was completely hooked on it. I thought the first person narrative added to the tension, of this particular story, as you could really imagine you were Nore going through all these terrifying experiences. I think this book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8557161482196380224">If I had to choose a favourite book, from my mid to late teens, this one would be a very serious contender. I recall picking this up, at the local library, imagining it to be some kind of history book from the title. It looked intriguing enough to take home and read so I did. I was completely hooked on it. I thought the first person narrative added to the tension, of this particular story, as you could really imagine you were Nore going through all these terrifying experiences. I think this book had a bit of everything; witchcraft, love, loss, romance, deception, blended family relationships, thrills and even some comedic moments. The description of teenage Josie, moody, fickle and trying so hard to be grown-up was spot on and heartbreakingly poignant after reading the climax. The doomed friendship between Nore and Gabe was also one of the highlights and the way the story cleverly unfolds from a seemingly ordinary tale of parental remarriage and the respective teenagers having to deal with this, to something altogether more sinister, is very well paced. I couldn't tell where this story was going to go, while I was reading it, which was very refreshing. I actually found myself biting my nails, as the book wound to its end, wondering whether Nore was going to escape with her life or not. If that isn't an indication that the book is a page turner I don't know what is. I highly recommend this one. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/388796-morgan?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/388796-morgan?shelf=odd-story" class="actionLinkLite">odd-story</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/388796-morgan?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/388796-morgan?shelf=revenge" class="actionLinkLite">revenge</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1257028252">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4672125199323543081">Locked In Time: Revenge can last forever...<br /><br />The Setup (Overview):<br /><br />A young woman named Nore is visiting her father for the first time since he remarried. The remarriage was something that took Nore by surprise since her mother had passed away not long before and her father still seemed to be lost in his grief. Though she did not entirely approve, Nore gave her father the benefit of the doubt as the new marriage seemed to pull him out of the depression that had consumed his life. In order to welcome</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4672125199323543081">Locked In Time: Revenge can last forever...<br /><br />The Setup (Overview):<br /><br />A young woman named Nore is visiting her father for the first time since he remarried. The remarriage was something that took Nore by surprise since her mother had passed away not long before and her father still seemed to be lost in his grief. Though she did not entirely approve, Nore gave her father the benefit of the doubt as the new marriage seemed to pull him out of the depression that had consumed his life. In order to welcome her into the new “family” and introduce her to her stepmother, Lissette, her father invites her to Louisiana to spend her summer vacation getting to know everyone at Lissette's family estate which is known as Shadow Grove. While the initial meeting is a bit tense, Nore soon finds that Lissette and her two children are not really that bad. Everything seems to be going well until Nore starts to notice that the family seems to be a little too out of touch with the modern world...<br /><br />The Story(Some Story Details):<br /><br />Nore first notices the time frame difference in conversations with the family. Lissette's children speak of events that happened twenty years before as if they saw what happened first hand. Yet one child is only twelve and the other is seventeen. There are other occurrences where people in town swear that they have seen Lisette before, somewhere. As Nore continues to investigate it seems that she is dealing with something that is not possible. What Nore doesn't realize is that some people make terrible mistakes and will do anything to keep those mistakes secret. Even if it means making sure that those that go snooping into the past will soon become part of it. <br /><br /><br />Conclusion(My Overall Opinion on the Story): <br /><br />This was a short, interesting read. The story flows well and for the most part makes sense. The characters are well written and even though the effects of what ails Lissette's family are not really explored in detail there are a few scenes with Lissette's children that do give a glimpse of what being “locked in time” has done to them. Even though Lissette's family has resigned themselves, mostly, to their fate; they do still try to give Nore a way out, even though she can't really take the offers because of her father. <br /><br />This is where I have a slight problem with the story though. Or maybe it just comes from having read other stories that are like this that have the room to explore that side of the story. I get that Nore, understandably, is not willing to give Lissette's family the benefit of the doubt due to the events of the story. Some of Nore's action's come across as tone deaf towards the end of the story to me though. Even though Lissette's children seem apathetic towards the events, they do *try*. Nore just kind of bats them away instead of trying to listen. In the end, strangely, Nore does do her best to help in a way. It just came across as too little, too late to me.<br /><br />In the end I do recommend giving this a read. I t does have a couple of twists in it and it does pack a lot in for a shorter story. I recommend this to anyone who likes supernatural mysteries, thrillers, and books where the “bad guys” might be worthy of some sympathy too. m.a.c</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9840093543942057157">Originally read? Reread 2014.<br /><br />This is a book I would think of every now and then, even though I couldn't remember the author or title. (Thank you to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/185-what-s-the-name-of-that-book">What's The Name of That Book???</a> group for helping me find it!)<br /><br />The story has been updated slightly, mostly addressing changes in technology.<br /><br />I enjoyed the story, but I have to admit after reading some other reviews they bring up good points about problems with the characters (Nore doesn't have much of a personality, there is a lot of focus on how f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9840093543942057157">Originally read? Reread 2014.<br /><br />This is a book I would think of every now and then, even though I couldn't remember the author or title. (Thank you to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/185-what-s-the-name-of-that-book">What's The Name of That Book???</a> group for helping me find it!)<br /><br />The story has been updated slightly, mostly addressing changes in technology.<br /><br />I enjoyed the story, but I have to admit after reading some other reviews they bring up good points about problems with the characters (Nore doesn't have much of a personality, there is a lot of focus on how females look as opposed to personality, one of the characters is racist and blames a woman for seducing her husband, which is a bit problematic when you apply historical knowledge of the time.)<br /><br />There's also this odd incesty relationship between Nore and her step-brother, Gabe. I mean, maybe people felt differently 30 years ago, or it's regional thing, but nowadays step-family is mostly regarded as family and being attracted to a step-sibling would be taboo.<br /><br />I think by far my biggest problem is with Nora's father, Chuck. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[After Nore's mother dies she is sent to a boarding school. Her Dad emails her that he has remarried. He emails her this info; he doesn't even call to tell her in person! It's not even been a year since her mother died. He invites her out for the summer and says he wants to spend time with her, but all he seems to do sit in his office and write. He harps on her to get along with her step-family, something she seems willing to try to do, but he won't listen to any complaints made against them. Also, even if it would be a bit hard to believe her step-brother tried to kill her, he completely dismisses it and doesn't even listen to her. Not to mention she almost died, and no matter what he believes <em>she</em> believes her step-family is trying to kill her, but he leaves her alone with them, <em>when she doesn't feel safe with them</em>, for a trip. Hell, he barely says goodbye to her and when she gets downstairs he's driven off. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Hmm, I'm actually liking this story less and less as I write this review. I mean, I liked it overall, but some of the problematic elements overshadow the book. I mean, I reread the book because I enjoyed it when I was younger, but I question if I would really like it at all if I hadn't read it when I was younger and less informed/critical. <br /><br />I do feel like the setting of this book, a large Civil War mansion in Louisiana, though not precisely remembered, left an impression on me. I've noticed that I will sometimes take a closer look at books, not necessarily generally in my normal interest, if the setting is Louisiana. I feel like this book, and Gambit from X-Men are the reason for that. <br /><br />I guess the best way to look at it is that this book left an impression on me, and upon rereading it it continues too, although not exactly for the same reasons.<br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2593444891826685802"><br /> This story takes place in Louisiana, at an old southern plantation. It is right out side of a town called merville<br /> The charicters are, Nore, Lis, Chuck, Gabe, Josie and Dave. Nore is the main chariter she is a young 16 year old girl. She is coming down to Louisiana from New England to meet her new stepfamily. Chuck is her father he is a famous author, after they wanted to make his big book (life in the fast lane) in to a screenplay for a movie he moves to Louisiana, and meets Lisette.<br />In locked</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2593444891826685802"><br /> This story takes place in Louisiana, at an old southern plantation. It is right out side of a town called merville<br /> The charicters are, Nore, Lis, Chuck, Gabe, Josie and Dave. Nore is the main chariter she is a young 16 year old girl. She is coming down to Louisiana from New England to meet her new stepfamily. Chuck is her father he is a famous author, after they wanted to make his big book (life in the fast lane) in to a screenplay for a movie he moves to Louisiana, and meets Lisette.<br />In locked in time the plot is, Nore goes to live with her dad and new step family. Nore thinks something's up with her new family but ignores it.she later puts the puzzle pieces together and finds out that in the 1800's Lisette ( her new stepmother) made a deal with a Cajun slave so that Lis and her children could live forever. Soon after that Lis and her son Gabe try to kill Nore in a fire but fail and in doing that they kill themselves. Leaving Nores stepsister Josie alone. Nore leaves to go back and live at her home in New England.<br /> I believe that the author is trying to tell you to not trust everyone, to keep your friends closes but to keep your enemies closer. Also that if you try you can survive anything. Also to fight your own battles just like Nore did. <br />I would recommend this book to everyone. It's fun and adventurise. It always keeps you interested. The suspense is thrilling. You get attached to the characters and you feel like you're a part of the book. In conclusion I really recommend this great</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1232043251393145710">The book ‘Locked in Time’ by Lois Duncan is one of my favourite mystery books. <br />The main character Nore, joins her father and her step-family for school holidays for the first time. Nore has a step-mother, step-sister, and a step-brother. Nore’s mother had died because somebody hit her with their car, her step-mother’s husband had died because he was really sick, and a step-brother had died a few years ago. Then Nore’s dad and her step-mother Lisette married. Then one day, Nore has a dream about her mother telling her to get out of the house because she is in big danger. Nore thinks that it’s not true because it’s just a dream but few days later, she has a dream about her mother telling her to get out of the house again. She noticed that something strange was going on because her step-brother Gabe didn’t help when Nore fell out of their boat. Gabe noticed already that she couldn’t swim but he didn’t help her. Finally, she realizes that her mother’s telling the truth and she thinks that somebody in the family is trying to kill her.<br />The most saddest scene was when they were saying that Gabe’s girlfriend died few years ago. They broke up but he was still sad about it so he always went out with a fuel can and a fishing gear and came back late.<br />I would really like to recommend this book to people who really love mystery books because as you read more, it gets very interesting. Even if you hate books like me, you can’t stop because this book just makes read more and more. Every time when you read a page, it makes you think a lot because it is so mysterious.<br /></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1350552118">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11778471173483139848">I am a huge fan of Lois Duncan, so I might be a little biased. What I like in a story is tension and suspense, and Lois definitely delivers both in this book. If you enjoy modern teen fiction, you'll probably not relate to the main character. She speaks and thinks in a much more mature manner than teens in real life. But in the 80s, that was acceptable for literature. I found it a little amusing that people who reviewed this book found the dad insensitive and uncaring.If he were to believe her a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11778471173483139848">I am a huge fan of Lois Duncan, so I might be a little biased. What I like in a story is tension and suspense, and Lois definitely delivers both in this book. If you enjoy modern teen fiction, you'll probably not relate to the main character. She speaks and thinks in a much more mature manner than teens in real life. But in the 80s, that was acceptable for literature. I found it a little amusing that people who reviewed this book found the dad insensitive and uncaring.If he were to believe her and take her out of the situation, there would be no story! The only part that I would have liked to have seen done differently is for the heroine to have rescued herself. It seems she had a lot of help. But in all, the story was well paced and suspenseful. A fun read. Much more interesting to me than a lot of the modern YA that I have read. But again, if you didn't grow up on 80s YA, you may have a tough time finding the main character credible because of the way she thinks and speaks. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/850097286?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 10, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5880337-keith" class="user" title="Keith">Keith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer850097286">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10370383127945554991">I was very impressed by this novel by Lois Duncan. Nore was very a very sympathetic character from the beginning, and having her thrown into a new situation allowed for us to naturally be introduced to a new location and characters with her. The setting was perfect for a tale of secrets slowly revealed, and her isolation was brilliantly handled. I also liked that Nore wasn't left in the dark too long about the mysteries going on with her new family. Too many times, truths are painfully obvious t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10370383127945554991">I was very impressed by this novel by Lois Duncan. Nore was very a very sympathetic character from the beginning, and having her thrown into a new situation allowed for us to naturally be introduced to a new location and characters with her. The setting was perfect for a tale of secrets slowly revealed, and her isolation was brilliantly handled. I also liked that Nore wasn't left in the dark too long about the mysteries going on with her new family. Too many times, truths are painfully obvious to the reader, while the main character stumbles along blindly looking more and more stupid as these glaring facts pile up. Duncan avoids this by having Nore pick up on things very quickly and investigate them when given the opportunity. Though the reality is hard to accept, she doesn't deny it to the point of it being ridiculous. My only complaint is that the conclusion seemed a bit rushed with the fate of two of the characters taking place off screen.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10370383127945554991">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4186498946606344528">While Nore was off at boarding school, her father remarried. During her summer vacation, she'll be spending time with her new family at a new home called Shadow Grove.<br /><br />It's nice enough. Her stepmother seems to be nice, as her does her two children. But Nore starts noticing something isn't right with her new family. They're hiding something and the longer she's at Shadow Grove, the more dangerous it becomes for her.<br /><br />The story is set in Louisiana and it definitely has that southern feel. When Nore g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4186498946606344528">While Nore was off at boarding school, her father remarried. During her summer vacation, she'll be spending time with her new family at a new home called Shadow Grove.<br /><br />It's nice enough. Her stepmother seems to be nice, as her does her two children. But Nore starts noticing something isn't right with her new family. They're hiding something and the longer she's at Shadow Grove, the more dangerous it becomes for her.<br /><br />The story is set in Louisiana and it definitely has that southern feel. When Nore gets to Shadow Grove, it is like being transported back into time with just how everything is described. It's quite neat.<br /><br />I liked Nore as a character, but I think it would have been nice to get to know her more. Even though the story is told through her view, I feel there wasn't quite enough told about her. But she is still a good character.<br /><br />I completely got wrapped up in the story. It was one of those books I couldn't wait to read what happened next. The story was good, it was perfect and I just loved it.<br /><br />The only thing I didn't like was Nore's dad. I understand he got remarried, he loved his wife and her two children. Nore gets to Shadow Grove and gets along well with her stepmother and stepsiblings. I'm not going to spoil what happened, but something did happen that made Nore realize what's going on. So, come on, Nore gets along well with her new family and when something happens, when she realizes she is safe, Nore tries to tell her dad. He doesn't listen! He takes it as she just doesn't like her stepmother because she misses her mother. If that were the case, she wouldn't have gotten along with her new family from the beginning. And when your daughter, who you have known her whole life, tells you something is wrong, you're just going to be a jerk? <br /><br />Nore's dad was my only problem with the book. Otherwise, it is great. The story is so good and it kept me on the edge of my seat.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9451420109861066093">I've read one of Lois Duncan's novels in the past and thought it was AMAZING!<br />I found this book at a used book store and decided to read it, and I'm so glad I did!<br /><br />This book was able to grasp and hold onto my attention throughout. <br />I think this may have been because of the characters. I even began to hate</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9451420109861066093">I've read one of Lois Duncan's novels in the past and thought it was AMAZING!<br />I found this book at a used book store and decided to read it, and I'm so glad I did!<br /><br />This book was able to grasp and hold onto my attention throughout. <br />I think this may have been because of the characters. Each character's personality seemed to flow off the pages of the novel and into reality. There were times when I found myself truely annoyed at Josie because of her 'pre-teen brat-like attitude'. I even began to hate Lisette as the story went on. <br /><br />I would ABSOLUTELY recommend this book to anyone who enjoys suspense, or is looking for a light read. <br /><br />*SPOILER*<br />However, I couldn't help but notice some similarities between this novel and others by Lois Duncan ( for instance, Killing Mr. Griffin). Although not immediately evident, I found many common components such as plot structure (in both novels, the protagonist is trapped in a fire only to be rescued by those in which her true loyalties lie). I guess it's not that much, but in a way, it hindered the experience of reading this book. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11582101585360523596"><pre>...</pre> You may think that eternal youth would be amazing and awesome. Well think again after reading this incredible book. I really enjoyed this fiction book of immortality. I couldn't stop reading this book and I think that anybody who likes creepy and dangerous flirting with immortality should absolutely read this book.<br /><br /><br /><pre>...</pre>Nore wanted to just spend a summer vacation in Shadow Grove with her dad and her new step family. But then she has suspicions that something is wrong with the family ,so she sta</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11582101585360523596"><pre>...</pre> You may think that eternal youth would be amazing and awesome. Well think again after reading this incredible book. I really enjoyed this fiction book of immortality. I couldn't stop reading this book and I think that anybody who likes creepy and dangerous flirting with immortality should absolutely read this book.<br /><br /><br /><pre>...</pre>Nore wanted to just spend a summer vacation in Shadow Grove with her dad and her new step family. But then she has suspicions that something is wrong with the family ,so she starts to gather information. Then she finds out something terribly unbelieveable. The type of conflict in the story is person vs. person because Nore is trying to unmask Lisette and her two childern. Nore is a pretty and clever seventeen year old girl who is trying to adapt into a new family. Chuck is the father of Nore. Lisette is the new wife of Chuck and the stepmother of Nore. Joise and Gabe are Lisettes' only two children who try to help Nore but always obey their mother to do horrible things.<br /><br /><br /><pre>...</pre> I liked the way the author changed the moods slowly because I thought that it made the book interesting and wanting the reader to know what was going to happen next. In the story Nore thinks that she's living with a normal family until her suspicions slowly start to rise. This book reminds me of another amazing book called Summer of Fear because the author also changes the mood slowly. Nore's problem also reminded me of the conflict from the book Summer of Fear because both characters in the book try to discover the horrible things that people arond them and close to their family do or are doing to their family.I think that this is a very brave thing to do and thats what I also enjoyed about both books.<br /><br /><br /><pre>...</pre> The character's motivation in both stories was to save their families and keep their family together. I think that its very interesting that the author put the responsibilty on a character that was not an adult and a girl , to save their family, because it would give the reader a different prespective of what a young girl would do in this situation. I was angry about Gabe wanting to kill Nore because I really thought that he was really in love with her . In the book Summer of Fear I also thought that the supposed cousin of the main character actually cared for her but it turned out that she didn't. I wish that Lisettee could've found a way to undo the spell so they could all be a family. I think that it would be a great ending but it didn't happen that way.<br /><br /><br /><pre>...</pre>Overall I think that this book is a great book, I loved it , it was stunning, dangerous, and creepy. From one through ten I'd rate this book with a ten because it was incredible and I love everything about this book. I'd recomend this book to whoever likes dangerous and creepy stories. So if you think immortal youth can be awesome, think again.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_605289144">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605289144" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5000091-charlene" class="left imgcol" title="Charlene"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452104530p2/5000091.jpg" alt="Charlene" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/605289144?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 29, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5000091-charlene" class="user" title="Charlene">Charlene</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer605289144">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4090416998356390552">Lois Duncan is an author I loved to read when I was a teenager. Her suspense stories always captured my imagination and kept me turning pages. The premise of this story has a supernatural element that is pretty easy to guess way before Nore suspects anything, but the suspense lies in how Nore will discover her stepfamily's secret and how will she be able to stop them. Although the mystery is a little predictable, I think the character building and the writing makes this a very engaging read.<br /><br />Nore</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4090416998356390552">Lois Duncan is an author I loved to read when I was a teenager. Her suspense stories always captured my imagination and kept me turning pages. The premise of this story has a supernatural element that is pretty easy to guess way before Nore suspects anything, but the suspense lies in how Nore will discover her stepfamily's secret and how will she be able to stop them. Although the mystery is a little predictable, I think the character building and the writing makes this a very engaging read.<br /><br />Nore is an intelligent, observant main character, not too snarky or witty, but very kind and relatable and in the beginning, although she is a little bitter about her father's remarriage, she makes an effort to bond with her new family. Her step siblings, Gabe and Josie, are both likable and fiery, emotional and kind and through them, you see the toll their secret has taken on their family. Gradually things unravel, and it is interesting to see how Gabe and Josie are changed by Nore's personality. Nore's father is perhaps the least defined character in this book because he is often out of the picture while he is so focused on writing his novel and ignoring Nore's suspicions. Which is necessary to the plot, but boy, did I want to knock some sense into Nore's dad!<br /><br />The writing builds up the atmosphere and the tension masterfully in this captivating and suspenseful read. I think the ending perfectly tied up all the loose ends and was true to the character arcs. I was nervous about being disappointed by the ending of this story because it seemed like it would be difficult to create a satisfying ending when so much was at stake and things looked so hopeless for Nore, but the ending is pretty much perfect.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4090416998356390552">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_185507346">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185507346" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/908751-jenny" class="left imgcol" title="Jenny"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1345237652p2/908751.jpg" alt="Jenny" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/185507346?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 16, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/908751-jenny" class="user" title="Jenny">Jenny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer185507346">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3111581347913699595">Interested by the summary, I grabbed it from a book sale for 50 cents. I started it with lower expectations - Duncan's books always have fascinating plots, but sometimes I can't handle the stress of reading them. This, however, seemed a departure for her writing. Nore's situation was incredibly realistic, and while you were scared it wasn't horror-movie scary, more shocking scary at the reality of what is possible. The romance isn't overdone, and the characterization was fantastic. When I finish</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3111581347913699595">Interested by the summary, I grabbed it from a book sale for 50 cents. I started it with lower expectations - Duncan's books always have fascinating plots, but sometimes I can't handle the stress of reading them. This, however, seemed a departure for her writing. Nore's situation was incredibly realistic, and while you were scared it wasn't horror-movie scary, more shocking scary at the reality of what is possible. The romance isn't overdone, and the characterization was fantastic. When I finished I mulled for days over other ways it could have ended and whether or not I liked how it finished. It can really get you thinking, and despite being so very very different from The Adoration of Jenna Fox, it makes you think in the same way, and perhaps could be a companion book for those that liked it. (Although this is more mystic than sci-fi.)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3111581347913699595">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_276783749">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276783749" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1317038-brent" class="left imgcol" title="Brent"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1413131038p2/1317038.jpg" alt="Brent" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/276783749?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1317038-brent" class="user" title="Brent">Brent</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11367001-locked-in-time" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer276783749">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12224243462408205485">This is the second book I've read by <a title="Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">Lois Duncan</a>. The first was <a title="They Never Came Home (Laurel Leaf Books) by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47754.They_Never_Came_Home__Laurel_Leaf_Books_">They Never Came Home</a>, which is a better book than this one. <a title="Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">Duncan</a>'s writing style is good in both books, but the plot of <a title="Locked in Time by Lois Duncan" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11367001.Locked_in_Time">Locked in Time</a> was too predictable. Both books use suspense throughout a large part of the book, but suspense only works if the book isn't predictable. Also, the main character fails to make several obvious decisions that would have gotten her out of her bad situation.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1026334119">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4707757433409561708">I was drawn to this book by I Know What You Did Last Summer and the atmospheric Louisianan plantation setting. The story is enjoyable, with an engaging heroine who has to deal with the challenge of her father remarrying into an enigmatic southern family. The suspense is there, although perhaps not taut enough by today’s standards.</span>

          </span>

      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PrI7MwC1odvzl8eJK0oYFcbW2M0KFHYERfV1MY8N2ABbZgTg8me1IX9PszJVK/6njyEb1EPJMa4v/HCjQ5guRQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XB96JlSl4qBz6ZB+2kxFo4/naHv//qH8Tbnlu6B7bl45y0X1pnf2Wv8x5MWkLaMRxhCrYrYj5lYnsOApbO6YGw==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">About Lois Duncan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan"><img alt="26819" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1197061058p2/26819.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer976407121615994431">Lois Duncan (born Lois Duncan Steinmetz, April 28, 1934) is an American writer and novelist, known primarily for her books for children and young adults, in particular (and some times controversially considering her young readership) crime thrillers. Duncan's parents were the noted magazine photographers Lois Steinmetz and Joseph Janney Steinmetz. She was born in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, but gr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText976407121615994431">Lois Duncan (born Lois Duncan Steinmetz, April 28, 1934) is an American writer and novelist, known primarily for her books for children and young adults, in particular (and some times controversially considering her young readership) crime thrillers. Duncan's parents were the noted magazine photographers Lois Steinmetz and Joseph Janney Steinmetz. She was born in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, but grew up in Sarasota, Florida. Duncan started writing and submitting manuscripts to magazines at the age of ten, and when she was thirteen succeeded in selling her first story.<br /><br />Duncan attended Duke University from 1952 to 1953 but dropped out, married, and started a family. During this time, she continued to write and publish magazine articles; over the course of her career, she has published more than 300 articles, in magazines such as Ladies' Home Journal, Redbook, McCall's, Good Housekeeping, and Reader's Digest. After her first marriage, which produced three children, ended in divorce, Duncan moved to Albuquerque, New Mexico, to teach journalism at the University of New Mexico, where she also earned a BA in English in 1977. In 1965 she married Don Arquette, and had two more children with him.<br /><br />Duncan is best known for her novels of suspense for teenagers. Some of her works have been adapted for the screen, the most famous example being the 1997 film I Know What You Did Last Summer, adapted from her novel of the same title. Other made-for-TV movies include Stranger with My Face, Killing Mr. Griffin, Don't Look Behind You, Summer of Fear and Gallows Hill.<br /><br />In 1989 the youngest of Duncan's children, Kaitlyn Arquette, was murdered in Albuquerque, New Mexico, under suspicious circumstances. Who Killed My Daughter? relates the facts and conjecture about the still unsolved case. <br /><br />Duncan's second bk about her daughter's murder, ONE TO THE WOLVES: ON THE TRAIL OF A KILLER, picks up where the first book leaves off and contains all the new information Kait's family has uncovered from private investigation. <br /><br />The 1971 children's book Hotel for Dogs was released as a theatrical movie in 2009, starring Emma Roberts. That book has now been republished by Scholastic along with two sequels, News for Dogs (2009) and Movie for Dogs (2010).<br /><br />Duncan's Gothic suspense novel, DOWN A DARK HALL, is being filmed for the Big Screen and will probably be released in 2016.<br /><br /><br />Follow Lois on Twitter: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/duncanauthor" target="_blank">http://twitter.com/duncanauthor</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=100000216477747&amp;ref=profile" target="_blank">http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?i...</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.kaitarquette.arquettes.com" target="_blank">http://www.kaitarquette.arquettes.com</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="976407121615994431">...more</a>

    </div>
